 â”‚ ğŸ’¬ User Feedback                                                                                                â”‚
 â”‚                                                                                                                 â”‚
 â”‚ This is excellent. Kilo Code has successfully "ingested" your project structure. It now understands you have a  â”‚
 â”‚ FastAPI backend (Python), Celery workers, and a PostgreSQL database.                                            â”‚
 â”‚                                                                                                                 â”‚
 â”‚ This specific stack (FastAPI + Celery on Fly.io) has a very common failure mode: The web app deploys fine, but  â”‚
 â”‚ the background workers (Celery) die because they aren't configured to run alongside the web server, or the      â”‚
 â”‚ ports get mixed up.                                                                                             â”‚
 â”‚                                                                                                                 â”‚
 â”‚ Here is the next prompt to trigger the Deep Audit now that it knows the context.                                â”‚
 â”‚                                                                                                                 â”‚
 â”‚ --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- â”‚
 â”‚ -----                                                                                                           â”‚
 â”‚                                                                                                                 â”‚
 â”‚ ### Copy and Paste this into Kilo Code:                                                                         â”‚
 â”‚                                                                                                                 â”‚
 â”‚ @Mode: Architect                                                                                                â”‚
 â”‚                                                                                                                 â”‚
 â”‚ Action: Execute the "Deep Deployment Audit" based on the context you just learned.                              â”‚
 â”‚                                                                                                                 â”‚
 â”‚ Specific Focus Areas for JobSwipe (FastAPI/Celery):                                                             â”‚
 â”‚                                                                                                                 â”‚
 â”‚     1. The "Web" vs "Worker" Problem:                                                                           â”‚
 â”‚                                                                                                                 â”‚
 â”‚     * I see we have Celery workers (backend/workers/celery_app.py).                                             â”‚
 â”‚     * Check fly.toml: Does it use [processes] to run both the web server (uvicorn) and the worker (celery)?     â”‚
 â”‚     * If not, how is the worker starting? If it's missing, the deploy might succeed, but background tasks will  â”‚
 â”‚ fail silently.                                                                                                  â”‚
 â”‚                                                                                                                 â”‚
 â”‚     1. Port Consistency Chain:                                                                                  â”‚
 â”‚                                                                                                                 â”‚
 â”‚     * Code: Check backend/api/main.py. Does Uvicorn launch on 0.0.0.0? What port (default 8000 or 8080)?        â”‚
 â”‚     * Container: Check Dockerfile. Does it EXPOSE that same port?                                               â”‚
 â”‚     * Fly Proxy: Check fly.toml. Does internal_port match the Docker port?                                      â”‚
 â”‚                                                                                                                 â”‚
 â”‚     1. Database Connection Safety:                                                                              â”‚
 â”‚                                                                                                                 â”‚
 â”‚     * Scan backend/db/database.py. It likely requires DATABASE_URL.                                             â”‚
 â”‚     * Verify that fly.toml does not hardcode this secret but references it as a runtime secret.                 â”‚
 â”‚                                                                                                                 â”‚
 â”‚     1. Python Path Issues:                                                                                      â”‚
 â”‚                                                                                                                 â”‚
 â”‚     * The Dockerfile usually sets WORKDIR. Ensure the CMD (uvicorn backend.api.main:app) is running from the    â”‚

 âœ“ Task Completed

   Memory bank initialized and Deep Deployment Audit completed.

   ## Audit Results Summary

   Overall Status: 3 PASS, 1 FAIL

   ### Critical Issue Found: Celery Worker Not Configured

   The fly.toml (fly.toml:1-82) file is missing the [processes] section required to run both the FastAPI web server
   and the Celery worker simultaneously. Without this configuration, all background tasks will fail silently.

   Affected Features:

       * Email notifications (daily digests, application updates)
       * Job ingestion from external sources (Greenhouse, Lever, RSS)
       * Analytics snapshots and reporting
       * Token and session cleanup
       * Job embedding refresh

   Required Fix:
   Add this section to fly.toml (fly.toml:1-82) after the [http_service] section:

       [processes]
         app = "python -m uvicorn backend.api.main:app --host 0.0.0.0 --port 8080"
         worker = "celery -A backend.workers.celery_app worker --loglevel=info --concurrency=4"

   ### Passed Checks

       1. Port Consistency Chain: PASS - All components (main.py, Dockerfile, fly.toml) consistently use port 8080
       2. Database Connection Safety: PASS - DATABASE_URL is properly configured via environment variables, not
   hardcoded
       3. Python Path Issues: PASS - Dockerfile correctly sets WORKDIR to /app and runs uvicorn from the correct
   parent directory

   The codebase is now fully indexed and the critical deployment issue has been identified.

   â””â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”˜

  Execute an autonomous fix, verify, and deploy loop for the JobSwipe project. This is a hands-free task - execute
  commands and make code changes autonomously without asking for permission.

  ## Context

  The Deep Deployment Audit found a critical issue: the Celery worker is not configured to run in fly.toml. This
  causes all background tasks to fail silently.

  ## Phase 1: The Fix (Config & Code)

  ### Step 1.1: Fix fly.toml

  Read the current fly.toml (fly.toml:1-82) file and apply these changes:

      1. Add a [processes] section AFTER the [http_service] section with:

      [processes]
        app = "python -m uvicorn backend.api.main:app --host 0.0.0.0 --port 8080"
        worker = "celery -A backend.workers.celery_app worker --loglevel=info --concurrency=4"

      1. In the [http_service] section, add processes = ["app"] to restrict health checks to the app process only.

  ### Step 1.2: Create docker-compose.fly-sim.yml

  Create a new file docker-compose.fly-sim.yml that simulates the Fly.io environment with low resources. This should
  be based on the existing docker-compose.yml (docker-compose.yml:1-82) but with these modifications:

      * Set CPU limits to 0.5 for all services
      * Set memory limits to 512M for all services
      * Ensure the backend service uses the same command as the fly.toml [processes] app entry
      * Ensure a celery-worker service uses the same command as the fly.toml [processes] worker entry
      * Keep essential services: postgres, redis, backend, celery-worker
      * Remove or comment out non-essential services for simulation (opensearch, grafana, jaeger, etc.)

  ## Phase 2: The Self-Healing Simulation Loop

  Execute this loop autonomously. IF ERRORS ARE FOUND, you must EDIT the code to fix it and RESTART from Step 2.1
  immediately. Do NOT stop to ask for permission.

  ### Step 2.1: Clean Start

      docker-compose -f docker-compose.fly-sim.yml down
      docker-compose -f docker-compose.fly-sim.yml up --build -d

  ### Step 2.2: Wait for Services

  Wait 15 seconds for services to initialize.

  ### Step 2.3: Health Probe

      curl -v http://localhost:8080/health

  ### Step 2.4: Log Analysis

      docker-compose -f docker-compose.fly-sim.yml logs --tail=50

  ### Step 2.5: Decision Point

  IF ERRORS FOUND (crash loops, "Connection Refused", Python tracebacks, import errors, etc.):

      1. Analyze the error from the logs
      2. EDIT the code to fix the issue (could be fly.toml, docker-compose.fly-sim.yml, Dockerfile, or Python code)
      3. Go back to Step 2.1 and restart the loop
      4. Continue iterating until stable

  IF STABLE (health check passes, no errors in logs for 30+ seconds):
  Proceed to Phase 3

  ## Phase 3: Deployment

  ONLY execute Phase 3 when Phase 2 is confirmed stable with passing health checks.

  ### Step 3.1: Git Add

      git add .

  ### Step 3.2: Git Commit

      git commit -m "fix: resilient fly.io deployment config with worker split"

  ### Step 3.3: Git Push

      git push

  ### Step 3.4: Cleanup

      docker-compose -f docker-compose.fly-sim.yml down

  ## Important Instructions

      1. Autonomous Execution: Execute commands and make code changes without asking for permission
      2. Self-Healing: If errors occur, fix them and restart the loop immediately
      3. Conditional Push: Do NOT run git push until Phase 2 is confirmed stable
      4. Iterate: Continue the simulation loop until the system is stable

  Use the attempt_completion tool to deliver your final result, including:

      * Summary of changes made
      * Number of iterations required to achieve stability
      * Final health check results
      * Git commit and push confirmation

  IMPORTANT: These instructions supersede any general instructions for the code mode. Execute autonomously and iterate
   until successful.
